UK | 1,912,000,000

France | 486,000,000

Italy | 198,000,000

Other Countries | 132,000,000

From this table, it can be seen that the amount repaid by each country to date is only about one-quarter of the war debt principal. It would be closer to the truth to say that it is repayment of interest rather than repayment of debt.

Currently, the issue of modifying war debts has sparked fierce debate in the United States. The arguments for and against it are nothing more than the following theoretical and practical opinions:

In theory, opponents of the modification say that: (1) One-quarter of the $11,565,000,000 of war debt was loaned to European countries after the peace treaty was signed. This amount was not used for war, but for the internal reconstruction of each country. (2) The original interest rate stated in each country's loan note was 5%. Now the United States has been lenient and reduced the average interest rate to 2.135%, so the sacrifice of the United States has been very significant. (3) The budgets of each debtor country for expanding military equipment in recent years far exceed the debt repayment budget, so they are not without the ability to repay the debt. Therefore, the United States should never make further concessions and re-sign the war debt agreement.

Those who support the modification argue as follows: (1) Although the debts that the United States loaned to European countries after the peace treaty were used for the internal construction of each country, the motive was that the United States wanted to maintain the purchasing power of each country in the United States in order to prevent the early arrival of an economic panic in the United States. If it were not for Hoover's suggestion to the U.S. government on this matter, the United States would probably no longer lend to other countries. (2) Although the average war debt interest rate is 2.135%, it is not low. (3) Even if each country does not expand its military equipment, it will have no surplus capacity to repay the war debt, because the current military equipment of each country is purchased on credit within its own country. (4) When the United States loaned money to each country in the past, it did not lend cash, but lent American goods at the highest prices. After the war, prices fell sharply, and each country unknowingly bore an increased burden, and the value of each country's currency also plummeted, further increasing the U.S. debt claims unknowingly. What sacrifice has the United States made? Therefore, the United States should theoretically modify the war debt agreement to reduce the unbearable burden of each debtor country.

In terms of practical opinions, there are the following two points: (1) From Wilson to the present, the U.S. authorities have all declared that war debts and reparations are two completely unrelated international transactions. Opponents of the modification now hold the same view. Supporters of the modification say that although these two items are not a single account in law, they cannot be separated in practice. When the victorious countries demanded reparations in the beginning, they intended to use them to offset war debts. Later, the Young Plan and the Dawes Plan all used war debts as a reference. Even the Lausanne Reparations Conference never failed to use war debts as a standard. Hoover's suspension of war debt repayments for one year because Germany was unable to pay reparations made the close relationship between the two even more obvious. Since then, Germany's ability to pay reparations is even more hopeless, so it is necessary to finally modify the war debts. (2) International trade is now declining, mainly due to the global economic depression caused by the European War. To save this panic, it is necessary to work hard on the two issues of reparations and war debts. If the United States is willing to reduce the burden of each country, the world economy can be expected to recover, and the United States' foreign trade, especially trade with Europe, can naturally increase sharply. The gains of the people and the government's income each year can be more than the war debts repaid by each country. Why be so fixated on the repayment of war debts? This is the opinion of those who support the modification. However, opponents say that the total amount of debt repaid by each country last year was only one-quarter of the total amount purchased from the United States, so each country has not reduced its purchasing power due to repaying war debts. (December 2nd)

The Northeast Problem and the League of Nations (10)

"The Japanese representative has submitted to the Executive Yuan the Japanese government's statement regarding the League of Nations Inquiry Commission's report. The Japanese government believes that the entire report, especially the factual part, is a valuable description of the Manchurian Incident. In many sections and even the entire report, the Japanese government completely agrees. The Japanese government is extremely grateful for the sincere and hard work of the Inquiry Commission and expresses its gratitude to the entire Inquiry Commission and its members. However, for the sake of honesty, the Japanese government deeply believes that if the Inquiry Commission could conduct a longer study of this incident, its inferences and conclusions in the report would be more complete and appropriate. Therefore, the Japanese government has made every effort to draft a statement to point out the contents of the report, and it is hoped that the members of the Executive Yuan can give it careful consideration and judgment. The report contains a lengthy description of the current situation in China, but Japan cannot agree with its optimistic and hopeful attitude. At the time of the Washington Conference in 1922, although the situation in China was not entirely satisfactory, Japan was still able to follow other powers in hoping that China could restore peace and unity as soon as possible. Although the situation at that time was worse than at the beginning of the Republic of China ten years ago, we still had expectations of progress. Today, ten years have passed easily, and China's situation not only has not progressed, but is even worse than in 1922. In all parts of China, we can see the forces of warlords seizing power. Outer Mongolia has been communized, Tibet is fighting against the central government, and Turkestan is completely isolated from nominal China. The National Government only controls a few provinces in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River with military force. Shandong is experiencing internal warfare, Sichuan is in chaos, and the Guangdong faction expresses an aloof and even hostile attitude towards the government. In addition, there is another dangerous plot, as mentioned in the report, which is the threat of communism. China did not have this threat at the time of the Washington Conference. It entered China in 1925, when the revolutionary leader Dr. Sun Yat-sen carried out the revolutionary movement with the help of Soviet Russian military supplies, money, and military propaganda experts. After the death of Dr. Sun, General Chiang Kai-shek rose to be the leader, disagreed with Red Russia, and expelled all Russian personnel from the country. Today, Chiang is still directing the anti-communist military operations in the heartland provinces of China such as Hubei, Fujian, and Jiangxi. However, the Kuomintang and the National Government still have not abandoned the principles that caused the powers to increase their troops stationed in Shanghai a few years ago. The stationing of European, American, and Japanese troops in China and the entry and exit of foreign warships in the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River have been going on for more than 30 years. The purpose of these foreign troops is not only to protect their overseas Chinese, but also to protect their old embassies in Beijing (now Beiping) and the current embassies in Nanjing. May I ask, within a country with a recognized government, do the diplomatic representatives sent by various countries need the protection of troops and warships? Is this not a unique situation in China? Is the stationing of foreign troops in China merely a formality? The gentlemen should still remember the attack on the consulates of various countries in Nanjing by troops belonging to the National Revolutionary Army in 1927. Since then, conflicts between foreign troops and Chinese troops and bandits have occurred from time to time. Under normal circumstances, the Japanese government's troops and warships stationed in China are not more than those of the British or American governments. However, the number of Japanese nationals in China is several times greater than the total number of nationals of other countries. Therefore, the Japanese government has made every effort to reduce its troop deployments in China. After the Kuomintang adopted a radical policy, the friendship between China and the powers did not advance towards friendliness. The report stated that "Because of the adoption of violent anti-foreign propaganda, it has been hindered, and it has been carried out wantonly in two special places, which has helped to create the current conflict situation. This is the use of economic boycotts and the intervention of anti-foreign propaganda in schools." It also stated that "Dr. Sun Yat-sen's doctrine is taught in all schools, and its authority is equal to that of the Confucian classics in the previous century. Dr. Sun's speeches are respected no differently from Confucius before the revolution. However, unfortunately, in the education of young people, the construction of nationalism seems to receive more attention than its destructive aspects. A flip through the textbooks of various schools will make the reader feel that the author intends to use the flames of jealousy to ignite patriotism, and wants to build personality on the psychology of hatred. This kind of violent anti-foreign propaganda initially started in schools, and then applied to all aspects of social life. As a result, it lures students to participate in political activities, and sometimes even leads to attacks on the bodies, homes, or government offices of various ministers and other officials, and attempts to overthrow the government." The Chinese National Government is deeply imbued with anti-foreign sentiment, and is making every effort to instill xenophobia into the minds of young people. Fifty million young Chinese have now been affected by radical ideas, which will inevitably create the most terrible problems in the future. The Chinese army has reached 2 million people, but only a very small number of them are well-organized and able to protect the country. The Chinese government also has a method of resistance that is different from armed resistance, namely the boycott movement. This movement is actually a hostile act that violates commercial and friendship treaties, and the result is worse than open warfare. Japanese nationals in China have endured this kind of pain for several years. Sometimes, due to economic oppression, they have even reduced the number of meals per day, and countless people have gone bankrupt as a result. This movement is not a natural movement of the Chinese people, but is promoted and organized by the Chinese Kuomintang and the National Government as a national policy to force foreign countries to give up their treaty rights. The countries of the world have recognized war as illegal. Then, why can't boycott movements, whether formal or informal, be regarded as illegal acts? Besides Japan, the United Kingdom and the United States are also affected by China's economic boycotts, but Japan suffers the most. The more tolerant Japan is towards the Chinese government, the more obvious and deep the hostility it receives. However, the Japanese government has no hatred for the Chinese people. The above points refer to the general situation in China. Now let's focus on Manchuria. Before Zhang Zuolin's death in 1928, there was no such economic severance movement in Manchuria. After Zhang Xueliang joined hands with the National Government, staff from mainland China went to Manchuria one after another to carry out anti-Japanese propaganda, claiming that Japan's interests in Manchuria should be recovered one by one, and that all the investments Japan had made in railways, mines, and other undertakings should belong to China. All kinds of propaganda pamphlets, posters, speeches, etc., emerged endlessly. Even Zhang Xueliang's 300,000 troops were swayed by this kind of thought. However, Japan has repeatedly stated that it will never give up its various rights and properties in Manchuria, and has formally warned Zhang Xueliang and declared to the world that Manchuria is of extreme importance to Japan in terms of its position and economy, so it cannot tolerate any changes in its special status there. However, Japan has no other intentions other than protecting its property and rights stipulated in the treaty, and is willing to recognize China's nominal national rights, and will do its utmost to maintain the open door and equal opportunity principles of international policy. Japan's patience can be said to have reached its limit, but it was not Japan's fault that the final split occurred. The September 18th Incident last year was just a phenomenon of patience reaching its extreme and finally breaking. The report stated that the bombing of the South Manchurian Railway tracks was not sufficient reason for military action. The bombing of the tracks, in itself, is a small point, but the background must be noted. If this incident did not occur on the night of September 18th and on another day, the Inquiry Commission's opinion could be considered correct. However, the existence of the facts is not so simple, and the tension of the situation and the excitement of emotions at that time must not be ignored. After the incident, the speed of the Japanese army's actions may seem strange to those who do not know the situation. In fact, Japan must have prepared for the crisis in order to deal with it. Therefore, Japan cannot agree with the point in the report that the military action taken by the Japanese army on the night of September 18th cannot be regarded as legitimate self-defense. In the memorandum of the U.S. Secretary of State Kellogg on June 23, 1928, regarding the right of self-defense, it was stated that the right of self-defense should be enjoyed by any country and is implied in any treaty. When the U.S. Senate passed the Kellogg-Briand Pact, it made a resolution stating that "The right of a country to use military force for self-defense may sometimes extend beyond the country's borders." In addition, British Foreign Secretary Chamberlain also stated in letters dated May 19 and July 18, 1928, that there are several places in the world whose safety is of special importance to the United Kingdom. Therefore, the British government cannot but declare that the British government cannot tolerate external interference in these places, and that protecting these places from foreign attacks is a method of self-defense for the British Empire. It was also stated that the meaning of the Kellogg-Briand Pact should be based on not restricting or impairing a country's right to self-defense. In addition, the French and German governments have made similar statements. The Japanese government also stated in a memorandum to the U.S. ambassador to Japan on May 26, 1928, that the U.S. government's proposal also recognizes that it does not include the denial of the right of independent countries to self-defense. Based on the above reservations, the Japanese government believes that the Japanese army's actions on September 18th were entirely out of self-defense and there is no doubt. Then why did Japan not submit the Manchurian Incident to the League of Nations for resolution? Japan's reasons are: (1) Japan's national sentiment cannot allow the Manchurian issue to be subject to external interference. (2) The League of Nations' actions are extremely slow. If the League of Nations resolves the issue, the suffering of Japanese nationals in Manchuria, including Korean nationals, will be incalculable. (3) There are points of psychological difference between Japan and the West. (4) The arrival of the September 18th Incident was unexpected. After it broke out, it was in a situation that could not be left to its own devices. As for the various points in the report regarding Manchuria, there are many that the Japanese government cannot agree to. The report stated that Manchuria is a part of China. In fact, Manchuria is only the private property of a royal family, and it still belonged to Manchuria until the beginning of this century. The Chinese government's administrative power has never actually reached Manchuria. This point has been detailed in the Japanese government's statement. The Inquiry Commission stated that restoring Manchuria to its original state cannot be considered a satisfactory solution. Japan completely agrees with this point. However, it absolutely cannot agree with the point that maintaining and recognizing Manchukuo cannot be considered satisfactory. We believe that the creation of Manchukuo is the only satisfactory solution to this case. If this is abandoned, the Far East incident will only tend to be more chaotic. The Inquiry Commission expressed doubts about the authenticity of the Manchurian independence movement. In fact, the organization of Manchukuo was not due to Japan's direction, but to the local people's aversion to chaos. The officials of Manchukuo are all well-known local figures. Therefore, the so-called lack of an independence movement before September 18th is not a fact. As for the instructions that Japanese military and civil officials must not participate in the new organization of Manchuria, they were indeed telegraphed to be followed by Foreign Minister Shidehara and Army Minister Minami on September 26th. The Inquiry Commission expressed optimism about the future of mainland China, but pessimism about the future of Manchukuo. Japan's opinion is the opposite. Although the establishment of Manchukuo has not exceeded eleven months, its achievements are already considerable. Since the collapse of the Qing government 20 years ago, Manchukuo has actually been the first civil governance organization in the region. If the new government did not have the presence of the Japanese army, it would be difficult to establish. But may I ask, if the Chinese National Government did not have the support of guns, weapons, and foreign personnel, could it exist in Nanjing? As for the various progress of Manchukuo, the Japanese government's statement has described it in detail, such as the increasing stability of the value of the central bank's currency, which is its most important aspect. As for the bandit suppression work, it has not yet been completely successful, but if it is given time, it will eventually be cleared. In short, Japan cannot be held responsible for the Manchurian Incident. Japan did not pursue such events, and if all of China or Manchuria could have a suitable government so that Japanese nationals could live and work in peace, these events would probably not have occurred. Japan is only taking natural action for self-defense, and the independence movement in Manchuria after Japan's action also naturally followed. The Japanese government's policies, hopes, and determination are all based on the four words of maintaining peace. Japan does not want to fight with any country, nor does it want any country's territory. Japan is not an aggressor. Japan sincerely cares about China's happiness. For decades, China's unfortunate situation has been a dangerous force for the world's future, and Japan's policies are actually sufficient to consolidate peace in the Far East. If the Western countries actually make contrary comments about Japan, then the reasons are something that Japan cannot understand."

Geneva has been very gloomy for several days, with rare glimpses of sunlight. On the evening of the Executive Yuan's meeting, there was heavy rain and biting cold winds, as if heaven was also expressing concern for the future of peace. (The End) (Sent from Geneva on November 21)

Burning of the Xiamen Siming Court

Sudden Fire in the Chief Judge's Office

Greatest Loss of Civil and Criminal Cases

Xiamen Correspondence: A major fire suddenly broke out at the Xiamen Siming District Court on the 18th, turning the entire magnificent building into rubble. Most of the court's files were also reduced to ashes. The Siming District Court building was constructed with three sections, each with two floors. The front building housed the High Court branch offices, the middle building contained the District Prosecutor's Office, the High Court Chief Judge's Office, the High Court Chief Clerk's Office, and the Records Office. The rear building housed the District Court Chief Judge's Office and the offices. The 18th was a Sunday, and most of the court staff were off duty as usual, with only a duty prosecutor and bailiffs remaining. Unexpectedly, at 2:40 PM, a fire suddenly broke out in the Chief Judge Chen Fuchang's office in the rear building. The rooms were all separated by wooden partitions, causing the fire to quickly spread to the roof and then to the middle building. The bailiffs on the lower floor, upon seeing the situation, shouted for help and reported to various fire brigades by telephone. Some went up to the middle building to move down the High Court files, while others struggled to move their personal belongings. However, due to the intensity of the fire, some of the High Court files could not be moved out and were burned. Some say the cause of the fire was a short circuit in the Chief Judge's office, but this matter is of great importance and cannot be confirmed without sufficient evidence. Soon, the Xiamen fire brigade, the Public Security Bureau, and various water dragons (firefighting pumps) rushed to the scene and tried their best to extinguish the fire. However, water was difficult to obtain there, causing the fire to spread to the front building. The fire brigades then quickly dismantled the firebreaks behind and on either side of the court and the neighboring buildings, and worked hard to carry water to extinguish the fire. Amidst the chaos, the heads of the four offices, the Public Security Bureau Chief Lin Zhencheng, and others led teams to the scene to direct everything. Second Company, Third Platoon Leader Huang Guangcan and others led four platoons of soldiers to guard the county government and Siming Prison, one platoon to guard the Boji Hospital, to prevent any unexpected events. The remaining platoon stood guard at both ends of the road, preventing idlers from entering the fire scene, so the order was not disrupted. When the fire first started, the flames soared into the sky. After being extinguished by the fire brigades, it was finally put out at 5:30 PM. High Court Chief Judge Wang Tingyi, Chief Prosecutor Chen Baozhu (Chen Bao Yu), Prosecutor Ouyang Han, Chen Xiaoshi, and others arrived after hearing the news, stood on the road watching the fire, and inspected the files abandoned on the roadside, bowing their heads in silence. It was finally discovered that the fire started in Chief Judge Chen's office in the rear building. Chen's servant Wei Qichang (from Fuzhou) and a Cantonese man (also Chen's servant, name unknown) were taken into custody. Later, bailiff Zheng Shihui and two others were also taken to the county government for investigation. At 6:00 PM, the fire brigades saw that the fire had been extinguished and returned to their respective teams. Unexpectedly, at around 9:00 PM, the fire reignited because the embers in the building had not been completely extinguished, so the fire brigades rushed back again and extinguished it at around 10:00 PM. The court building had completely turned into a rubble field. In terms of losses, in addition to the entire court building being burned down and neighboring buildings being dismantled, the personal belongings of the staff were difficult to investigate. It was also heard that all the files of the District Court were destroyed in the fire, and the property deeds of the merchants and residents that were registered with the court were also burned. Now that the court has been burned down, the staff have no place to stay, so they are temporarily staying at the Wuzhou Hotel or friends' homes.

It is also reported that in this fire at the Siming Court, the High Court, being separated by a building, suffered the least loss. The District Court Prosecutor's Office and the place where the fire started were in the same row and were wooden buildings, so there was no way to save them. Only a few execution cases and ongoing cases from the clerk's office were rescued from the fire. The District Court had no losses in the general affairs and accounting sections of the court, but no civil or criminal cases were spared. The loss in civil cases is not counted. Fortunately, the registry was outside and was preserved. On the 20th, the District Prosecutor's Office began working temporarily at the nearby Ziyang School, and the High Court began working at the Siming County Government. It is unlikely that the High Court will find a new location temporarily. The District Court Prosecutor's Office is looking for a place to rent a house to work behind the Fourth Police Station. (December 21st)

The Third Day of the Jiangsu Provincial Assembly

The third Jiangsu Provincial Representatives' Conference was originally scheduled to hold its first formal meeting this morning (the 27th), but because the number of representatives present did not reach the legal quorum, it was changed to 3:00 PM in the afternoon. There were 126 representatives present. The chairman was Gu Ziyang. After the ceremony, Gu Zhutong first reported on the important work of the provincial government over the past year. After the report, Chen Dangyi, a representative from Tongshan County, stood up to question the establishment of a drug investigation office and the opium monopoly. Other representatives also stood up to ask questions. After Gu Zhutong took the stage twice to explain, he said that the establishment of the drug investigation office was solely responsible for investigating drugs and that there was no opium monopoly. He also said that he cherished the past revolutionary history and did not want this kind of incident to happen. Next, Zhao Qilu, the head of the Department of Civil Affairs, and others reported on their work in turn, and the meeting adjourned.

Court Service of Judgments in the Songjiang Bank Case

Creditors Will File an Appeal

After some creditors in the Songjiang Bank bankruptcy case entrusted lawyers Qu and Liu to file a civil payment lawsuit, the county court summoned them six times. The debate ended on December 6, and the public notice was announced on the 12th. The creditors believed that there were doubts and applied for an explanation, but no ruling was received. Yesterday (the 26th), Bai Guanlan and others received the county court's ruling. It is said that an appeal will be filed. The main text and reasons for the ruling are recorded below: "Main text" The plaintiff's lawsuit against the defendants Zhu Hesun and Gu Jiaxuan is requested to be withdrawn. The rest is deemed withdrawn. The plaintiff bears the litigation costs. "Reasons" The subject matter of the lawsuit must be determined jointly for each person in a joint lawsuit. If the other party's actions against one of the joint litigants are the same as those against the entire group, this is clearly stipulated in Article 53, Section 2 of the Civil Procedure Law. The so-called must be determined jointly means that the majority of private law relationships in substantive law maintain the same state for each joint litigant. Therefore, the other party's actions against one of the joint litigants should be regarded as the same as those against the entire group, in order to achieve this purpose of joint determination. In this case, the plaintiff stated that although Songjiang Bank adopted the form of a company, with directors, supervisors, presidents, managers, and treasurers, it was actually a partnership shop. The defendants shared the above-mentioned positions, or handled affairs on a regular basis, or participated in meetings. In essence, they were shareholders and important employees who performed duties. The bank suddenly declared a cessation of business and maliciously owed huge sums of money. The plaintiffs were either savings, deposits, or had excess transactions. They were all hard-earned money and necessary for life. Xie Liangda fled and could not be seen, so a public notice should be served. However, this case urgently needs to proceed. According to the company's regulations, directors and supervisors are all important employees and bear full responsibility. It is proposed to advance the trial, etc., and request joint compensation for debts. All the defendants Zhang Xiaomei and others are constituent elements of Songjiang Bank. The reasons for the lawsuit are the same in fact and in law. Regardless of whether the nature of Songjiang Bank is a company or a partnership, the defendants should be jointly responsible (Articles 28 and 681 of the Civil Code). It is necessary to maintain the same state in substance. Therefore, the defendant's lawsuit is an indivisible joint lawsuit. The plaintiff is an integral part of it. The plaintiff's withdrawal of the lawsuit against the defendants Zhu Hesun and Gu Jiaxuan (directors and supervisors) during the verbal debate should be regarded as a withdrawal against the entire group. However, the plaintiff's legal establishment of the creditor's rights will not be affected by the declaration of this ruling, and the substantive rights will not be affected. Combined explanation, based on the above conclusion, a ruling should be made in accordance with Article 12 of the Implementation Law of the Civil Procedure Law and Article 85, Paragraph 1 of the Civil Procedure Law, as in the main text.

Suzhou Anti-Japanese Association Intercepts a Large Batch of Enemy Cloth

After the Northeast Anti-Japanese Dare-to-Die Corps came to Suzhou, their work became quite tense. Although the shops did not dare to openly sell enemy goods, they still smuggled them into Suzhou. The Anti-Japanese Association received a tip that a large batch of enemy goods was being transported to Suzhou for sale. The association sent personnel to various water and land terminals to check. That night, at the intersection of Loumen Baihe Lane, they intercepted two large carts of Yanghe brand white twill enemy cloth secretly transported by Jiufeng Foreign Goods Store on Lindun Road, totaling forty bolts. The carts were sealed and stored by the Anti-Japanese Association for a scheduled meeting to punish the treacherous merchants and serve as a warning.

Robbery Occurs in Shenjia Village, Wuxi

In Shenjia Village, District 15, Tu 82, in the county, there is a Shen Hanchu family who are fairly well-off. His son works in a hardware store in Shanghai. He returned to his hometown the day before yesterday, carrying 500 silver dollars to prepare to buy farmland. Unexpectedly, the bandits found out about it and suddenly came to rob last night. In addition to being robbed of 500 silver dollars, there were also two gold rings, two pairs of gold bracelets, and two coats, totaling more than 700 silver dollars in losses. In Zhang Xiaolong's home in Xiaozhang Lane, District 3, the villagers received 200 silver dollars in savings the day before yesterday, which the bandits learned about. At about 2:00 AM last night, six or seven bandits robbed the house, taking two gold-inlaid gemstone rings, a pair of gold bracelets, five silver dollars, and six or seven pieces of clothing, totaling more than 200 silver dollars in losses.

Jiading Police and Militia Arrest Five Thieves

The other day, Chen Jinsheng, a farmer from Xishenjia Stone Bridge, Zhensheng Hall, wanted to buy the farmland next to his house and borrowed silver dollars from others. The nearby bandits Lu Jinsheng and others learned about it and took advantage of the fact that the money had been borrowed but not yet paid. They ganged up and went to rob, losing more than 100 silver dollars in cash, dozens of dollars worth of jewelry and clothing, etc. After the report was made to the county government for arrest, Wang Bingxun, the director of the Nanxiang Public Security Bureau, and Cheng Hanmin, the head of the Second District Militia, arrested five thieves, Chang Jinsheng, Wang Ayun, Wang Bingsheng, Zhu Xiaodi, and Wang Jinsheng, in Dahu and sent them to the county for legal proceedings.

Bandits Rob and Injure People on the Road

Dai Wenliang, from Pengmen Village outside the West Gate, was working as a clerk in Xu Tongyuan's rice shop in Waigang. On the 25th, he collected payment for goods at the Dalong Shop in Jiading. It was near dusk when he returned via Liuliting. Four bandits blocked his way, wielding sharp knives and stabbing Dai several times. Dai fainted immediately, and all the 400 silver dollars he had were robbed. Dai woke up several hours later and called for help, but the bandits were gone.

Zhenjiang Jinsheng Money Shop Suddenly Runs Aground

The Zhenjiang Jinsheng Money Shop has been open for more than 30 years and has a good reputation. The initial capital was only 500 yuan, but today it has exceeded one million. Two Robberies in Changshu in One Night

Nanhengjing, near Pingshu in District 14 of the county, is a small town with few residents and no defenses, so it is easy for bandits to mix in. At about 12:00 AM the night before last (the 24th), more than a dozen bandits suddenly arrived in the town to rob. At that time, the residents of the town were asleep. The bandits first went to Xu Lian's house to rob, losing a pair of gold bracelets and more than 50 silver dollars, as well as clothing, etc. Then the bandits went to the homes of Xu Guisen, Yang Arong, and others one after another to search and rob, and the losses were also considerable, totaling no less than a thousand silver dollars. In Baiai Township, District 10, at about 1:00 AM on the 24th, five or six bandits landed on the shore from the Baiyuankou River and went directly to the home of Deputy Township Chief Lu Fenglan, broke into the house, searched and robbed for an hour before escaping. They were robbed of 122 silver dollars in banknotes, 42 silver dollars in cash, 12,000 copper coins, and more than 20 pieces of single-layer and cotton clothing. Afterwards, people were sent to report to the police teams in Zhoushi and Wushi. By the time the police arrived, the bandits were gone.

An Old Man of Ninety-Three

Mr. Ma Xiangbo's Radio Broadcast

All Compatriots Throughout the Country, Help the Northeast Volunteers

A Mandatory Donation of One Copper Coin Per Person Per Day

Yesterday morning at 10:20 AM, the Northeast Refugee Relief Association specially arranged for Mr. Ma Xiangbo to broadcast a radio speech to help the Northeast Volunteers. The Ya Mei Company specially installed equipment at Mr. Ma's residence in Xujiahui. The sound was very clear at that time, and his speech was very touching. The record is as follows:

Everyone, it's getting late, wake up. It has been a full year and three months since the September 18th Incident last year. When the Japanese government launched the incident, it expected that China had no ability to resist and could easily take it in one go. The formal army was indeed what they expected. But they never expected that the people of the Northeast would rise up to resist on their own. They may have expected that, like when they annexed Korea before, they would only need to mobilize a small number of troops and it would be pacified in two or three months at most. They never expected that fifteen months later, the people's resistance not only did not decrease, but increased and expanded compared to before. This is really something they did not expect. However, everyone, we should not be happy about this, let alone take pride in it. Why is it not enough to be happy about? Because when the incident occurred, the Japanese army was somewhat contemptuous of the enemy. They regarded our Northeast Volunteers as bandits, thinking that they would not be defeated in one battle. Since these fifteen months, they have not only not gained any advantage, but have often failed. Their attitude towards the volunteers has changed to very serious, and their methods have become more vicious. They are now using their superior weapons and openly violating international conventions, using poison gas. They used to only want to threaten the people of the Northeast, but now they want to eliminate them. Therefore, the more the Japanese army cannot gain an advantage in the Northeast, the greater the danger of the Northeast Volunteers' future. How can we be complacent about small victories? Why is it not enough to be proud of? Everyone, think about it. The three words "non-resistance" lightly gave away thousands of miles of territory. If it were not for the people of the Northeast, the farmers, workers, and merchants, who rose up to save themselves, the three northeastern provinces would have become the second Korea long ago. Who is the glory of this fifteen months of arduous struggle? The Shenbao of the 23rd of this month published a piece of news about the volunteers. It is said that Feng Zhanhai's troops had no choice but to retreat westward because they ran out of ammunition and supplies. When crossing the river, the families of the officers and soldiers at all levels were unable to escape back to Guan Nei beforehand. It was inconvenient to take them with them, and they were afraid that they would be trampled on by the Japanese if they were left behind. Speaking of a very painful thing, there were even those who killed their wives before leaving. Everyone, who doesn't have a wife? Killing their wives for no reason, for what? Yesterday's newspaper also said that the volunteers mostly slept in the wild, without clothes to keep out the cold. Everyone wrapped some firewood or carried a saddle. Without food, they could only fill their stomachs with grass roots and tree bark. Everyone, who is this for? Can we still be safe and sound if they all die? After the three northeastern provinces are lost, can Guan Nei still be as stable as Mount Tai? Therefore, when I read the news about the volunteers in the newspaper, I feel that now Japan is using the power of the whole country to eliminate the volunteers. If the volunteers do not receive a steady stream of supplies, they will definitely be eliminated. At the same time, I feel that the people of the Northeast are eating their own food and risking their own property and lives to fight for these thousands of miles of territory for the country. Now they are using their flesh and blood to block the artillery fire, and even their food and clothing are not sufficient. Are we still living in peace and enjoying ourselves? How can we be worthy of them? Looking back at Japan over the decades, they have been painstakingly calculating China. Since the September 18th Incident, although they have encountered an extreme economic panic, they are still united and dealing with the current difficult situation. Compared with our numb attitude, there is really nothing to say. Is China really going to perish? Therefore, we have only two feelings for the volunteers, namely "fear" and "shame." If we want to get rid of "fear," we must do our best to help them. They exist. One day, the Republic of China will not perish for one day. If we do our best to help the volunteers, we will fulfill a share of the responsibility of saving the country and reduce a share of the guilt in our conscience. I think the easiest way is for us to start today, no matter who, regardless of age or gender, to save one copper coin every day, and then hand it over to the place that receives donations after accumulating a whole number. Everyone, on the road or at the door of your house, which day and where do you not spend two more copper coins? When you meet a beggar, you still throw a copper coin to him. The Northeast Volunteers who are wrapped in firewood and eat grass roots and tree bark cannot be compared to disaster victims and beggars. Donating to charity is still worth ten or eight yuan, but one copper coin a day, shouldn't it be worth it? I personally have made up my mind to do this. Although I am old, one year is more than a block of money. Everyone is of course much younger than me, and of course will accumulate more than me. If everyone can do this, we will have no use for "panic" and "shame." (The old man paused here and continued),

Everyone, wake up. If there is gunpowder next to the pillow, can we sleep? If there is a small thief in the house, can we sleep? Japan has accumulated decades of ambition and attempts to poison us, to occupy our territory, not only the three northeastern provinces, not only the Yangtze River area, half of the country is full of spies, and there are even accomplices to help him. Only the Northeast Volunteers are worthy of world justice. Think about it, the traitors who "eat human flesh on the land" can still make absurd arguments on the League of Nations seat. Does the world still have "humanity" and "human heart" justice? The people of Jiangsu and the people of Shanghai were able to bravely resist Japan with the 19th Route Army when the planes were overhead and the flames of war were on the ground, fighting for the country's personality. Now the whole country should help the Northeast Volunteers and preserve justice for the world. I hope that parents will lead the family, shopkeepers will lead the employees, factory owners will lead the factory workers, and various groups will implement the national mandatory donation of "one copper coin per person per day" from today. First, it shows the spirit of national cooperation and facing national disasters together with the Northeast Volunteers. Second, it proves that our country is unyielding, because one copper coin per person per day is 470 million per day. If we use the same spirit to strive for self-reliance, then Japan's ambitions for aggression will eventually fail. In short, this start of not forgetting to save the country every day and everyone helping the Northeast's daily donation movement means that we all have a conscience, have the ability, and that the whole country, all sectors, unite and strive for survival, defend ourselves for humanitarianism, and will eventually have a day to recover the lost territory of the Northeast.

This manuscript is a record of the broadcast, which was read and approved by Mr. Xiangbo. Recorded by Xu Jingxian at Leshan Hall

External Telegram, Yu Ming et al. Extend Welcome

National Goods Year's New Year's Day Grand Automobile Parade

Parade Route Passes Through the Chinese City, the French Concession, and the International Settlement

Domestic Factories, National Goods Stores, Organizations, and Individuals All Participate

The Shanghai Local Association, the Shanghai Machine-Made National Goods Factories Association, and the China National Goods Production and Sales Cooperation Association, the three organizations that initiated the National Goods Year's New Year's Day Automobile Parade, have set up a preparatory office on the second floor of the Dalu Department Store on Nanjing Road, inside the China National Goods Company. Parade guidelines have been printed for participants to read. Registration began yesterday, and the enthusiasm of local national goods factories and national goods stores to sign up has been extremely high. Banking Association Organizes Clearing House

Thirty Members Have Joined

The Banking Industry Association, in view of the increasing development of the banking industry and in order to facilitate the collection and settlement of funds among banks, has resolved through a meeting to organize a clearing house. Since the preparation, it has been nearing completion. It has been decided to submit it for discussion at the general meeting of members at 4:00 PM today, with the intention of opening on January 10, 1933. The details are recorded as follows:

Preparations Nearing Completion

The clearing house, after being actively designed and prepared by Zhu Puquan, the manager of the joint preparatory committee of the Banking Industry Association, and others, the clearing house's articles of association have been formally passed. According to Article 3 of the articles of association, all member banks of the association and committee banks of the joint preparatory committee shall join as clearing banks. Other banks or trust companies in Shanghai may join with the introduction of two or more clearing banks and the approval of the committee bank representatives' meeting. As of yesterday's deadline, a total of thirty banks have joined, including twenty-six committee banks such as Bank of China, Bank of Communications, Xingye Bank, Industrial Bank, Zhongfu Bank, and Siming Bank, and four non-committee banks such as the Silk and Satin Industry Bank. As for all preparations, they are nearing completion.

Address Determined

The address of the clearing house has been decided to be at No. 4 Hong Kong Road, downstairs in the Banking Association building, the former site of the National Debt Fund Custody Committee. Decoration began the day before yesterday. After the opening in the future, the exchange time will be from 11:00 AM to 11:30 AM for the first time and from 3:20 PM to 3:50 PM for the second time every day, except Saturdays, Sundays, and public holidays. On Saturdays, it will be from 12:30 PM to 1:00 PM for the first time and from 3:20 PM to 3:50 PM for the second time. If the balance of the clearing bank's transactions is insufficient to pay, the amount due shall be made up before 4:30 PM on the same day.

Opening Soon

A reporter from the Xin Sheng News Agency interviewed Lin Kanghou, the Secretary-General of the Banking Industry Association, yesterday. According to him, Zhu Puquan, the manager of the joint preparatory committee, will concurrently serve as the manager of the clearing house. The opening date is around January 1933, after the New Year's holiday. It must await the decision of the Banking Industry Association's general meeting of members on the 28th. After implementation, it will be very convenient for banks to collect and settle funds. There is no need to settle in cash, only clearing of checks is required. Moreover, various European and American countries have already established them. Now, we are starting with the member banks of this association and the committee banks of the joint preparatory committee. All foreign banks and Chinese money shops can join voluntarily. However, according to reliable information, it has been decided to open on January 10, 1933.

General Meeting Today

The Banking Industry Association is scheduled to hold its general meeting of members for the second half of 1932 at 4:00 PM today in the hall at No. 4 Hong Kong Road. In addition to reporting on the work in the second half of the year, the meeting will discuss the budget and final accounts for 1933, the organization of the clearing house, the election of officers, and the opening date, etc.

Silver and Money Industries Express Views on Shipment of Silver Dollars to the Northeast

Supplementing Finance, No Other Effect

The recent large-scale shipment of silver dollars from this city to the Northeast has attracted attention from all sectors. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce has sent letters to the silver and money industries to inquire. The following are the details learned by reporters from the Xin Sheng News Agency who went to the silver and money industries to inquire:

Banking Industry: Mr. Lin Kanghou, the Secretary-General of the Banking Industry Association, said that the Northeast has abundant resources, reaching the whole country. The total amount of soybeans and sorghum transported to the south each year is about 20 to 30 million yuan. This time, the banking industry's shipment of silver for export is purely commercial in nature, such as: ㈠ After the Three Northeastern Provinces were occupied by Japan, our country has never recognized the puppet state. Therefore, the sorghum and soybeans produced there are still national goods. If merchants purchase them, they must use silver dollars. ㈡ Since the September 18th Incident, the Chinese banks in the Three Northeastern Provinces, the local residents do not trust banknotes and hoard silver dollars. For deposits, they withdraw them together. In fact, it is necessary to transport silver there to supplement them. In short, the banking industry's shipment of silver for export has no other effect. Moreover, commercial firms and foreign banks are the most likely to ship silver for export.

Money Shop Industry: Mr. Qin Xieqing, the Secretary-General of the Money Shop Industry Association, said that commercial firms ship the most silver dollars to the Three Northeastern Provinces. Since the money shop industry has no branches there, there is no need to transport silver there to supplement them. Commercial firms purchase silver dollars from money shops. Under the circumstances of depression in various industries, money shops have long stopped lending. Therefore, silver must be exchanged for silver dollars. This exchange is purely commercial in nature. For example, since there is a large amount of silver exported, the silver rate will inevitably be tight. Today (i.e., yesterday), the silver rate was 7 qian, 1 fen, 4 li, and 625 si in the morning, and 7 qian, 1 fen, and 4 li in the afternoon, which is slightly the same as before. It can be seen that there is a large amount of silver stored in this city, which is a phenomenon due to the sluggishness of industry and commerce in various places.

Ministry of Railways Strictly Restricts Free Train Rides

Strictly Verify Official Travel Passes

Directors Huang of Both Railways Issue Circulars for Notification

The Ministry of Railways believes that various free official travel passes are issued without restriction, which wastes railway funds and has a significant impact, especially on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway Bureau. Often, the first-class seats are almost entirely free tickets, and even additional carriages are added, but most of them are not truly necessary for official business. What is even more hateful is that they even carry people without tickets, occupying seats, which makes it difficult for paying passengers to find seats. This kind of treatment is extremely unfair, causing outside complaints. The railway bureau privately issues various long-term free passes without standards. When checking tickets, they do not verify the photos or ask about job titles. They simply glance at the red pass and let them pass. Therefore, there are often situations of borrowing. In addition to the staff of the ministry and railway departments, there are also other government officials and private individuals who obtain free passes by currying favor with important officials of the ministry and railway departments. Railway staff often bring relatives and friends to ride the train without tickets. The corruption of railway affairs can be said to have reached its extreme. These people who abuse their power, disrupt railway discipline, and erode railway administration have become accustomed to it and are shameless. The true customers of the railway, the passengers who pay for tickets, are inconvenienced as a result. There is nothing more unfair than this. It is now heard that the ministry intends to correct the abuses and rectify passenger transportation.

A general order has been issued to all railways that, except for railway staff who need to travel on official business, no long-term free passes of any kind shall be issued. Furthermore, the official travel passes for the ministry's staff have also been strictly regulated. They must be issued only if they are indeed on official business and comply with the regulations. It is also heard that the long-term passes for the Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Bureaus that have already been issued in advance for use next year have also been ordered by the ministry to be invalidated.

The Ministry of Railways, in view of the past abuses in issuing free tickets by the two railways, which is contrary to the original intention of reorganization and revival, has instructed the Business Department to formulate strict restrictions and has telegraphed Directors Huang of both railways to comply. All free travel permits for 1933, except those that are truly necessary for official business and have been submitted to the ministry for approval before being issued, shall be issued later. Those that have already been issued shall be invalid. It is heard that the railway bureau has received the ministry's telegram and has issued a circular for notification.

County Government Plans to Build Granaries for Grain Storage

Three Methods Agreed Upon

The Shanghai County Government believes that the matter of grain storage is related to the important political task of preparing for famine. Recently, it has also received orders from the provincial government urging the construction of granaries. However, the county's public funds are extremely stretched. Therefore, County Magistrate Yan sent a letter to the Bean and Rice Industry Association of the urban area requesting donations for grain storage. The association generously donated 10,000 yuan in foreign currency, which, together with other funds, totaled 15,000 yuan. County granaries can be built. Therefore, at 10:00 AM yesterday, the second committee meeting of the County Granary Grain Management Committee was convened. The committee members present were County Magistrate Yan, Wang Huazhao (substituting for Wang Juntang), Zhang Jingye, Jiang Shijie, and Zhang Yi. Ye Dezhen, the county secretary, attended as an observer. Four committee members, including Kang Yongnian, were absent. More than half of the legal number were present. Chairman Yan, the committee member, and recorder Hu Gongshou, after the chairman reported on the agenda, proposed the construction of the county's grain storage granaries. After discussion, three methods were resolved: ㈠ Distribution of funds: 7,000 yuan for building granaries in the new county seat, and 8,000 yuan for preparing to purchase grain. ㈡ Location of the granary base: Determined to be north of Tangbei Road and west of Hengli in the new county seat, purchasing 5 mu of land. ㈢ Appointing members to prepare: Appointing the three standing committee members Yan (Yu), Jiang (Shijie), and Zhang (Jingye) and committee member Zhang Yi and Director of the Construction Bureau Sun to actively plan and handle the matter.

Municipal Bureau of Public Works Dredges Yuan Chang River

Public Notice No. 194 of the Municipal Bureau of Public Works: Public notice regarding the dredging of the Yuan Chang River. The Yuan Chang River is an important waterway in the northwest of the city center. Due to the fact that it has not been dredged for many years, the riverbed is silted up and shallow. In addition, there is a great need for earthwork for the road and foundation projects in the second reclamation area in the city center. It is proposed to excavate in the river. The municipal meeting has resolved to dredge the river. Now, this river project is about to begin. The Land Bureau has sent personnel to measure the land. In the future, the parts of the river that need to be curved and straightened, and require private land, will be purchased at a fair price. A public notice is hereby issued to inform the villagers.

Survivors of the Sinking of the New Futai Ship Can Arrive in Shanghai Today

All Thirty-Four People Transported by the Tongshun Ship

The New Futai Ship of the Heping Shipping Company, managed by the Futai Shipping Co., Ltd., ran aground and struck a reef on the Tongsha sea area on the morning of the 26th. The entire ship sank, causing great losses. The crew members and sailors were rescued by the Tongshun ship and can come to Shanghai today. Further details are recorded below:

The Ship Sinks to the Bottom of the Sea

The New Futai Ship struck a reef at 4:45 AM on the 26th. Initially, only the third cabin was breached. However, since the damaged area was below the waterline, seawater flooded the cabin. After 10:00 AM, the engine room was also affected. When the engine room flooded, the boiler went out, and the ship could not move. The telegraph was also out of service. The ship sank directly into the sea. By noon, the entire ship had sunk into the sea. Yesterday, the company received a telegram stating that only a small section of the chimney was visible at low tide. The pilot platform, main building, etc., were all submerged in the sea. The ship could not be seen when the tide rose.

Rescue of the Crew

When the ship was sinking, the shipowner, K. S. Mun, the chief officer, the second officer, the chief engineer, and others first ordered all the sailors to leave the ship and escape in lifeboats. The last to leave the ship was the shipowner. The crew members drifted in the sea and were seen by the Taizan Maru ship of the Japanese Osaka Company, which rescued 24 of the crew members and sailors. There were also 10 sailors, stokers, etc., who escaped by sampan and were rescued by the pilot boat there. Therefore, all the crew members were rescued.

Tongshun Assists in Rescue

The Datong Company's Tongshun ship was transporting coal from Hongji to Nanjing this time. On the 26th, it passed through Tongsha and heard about the New Futai's accident. The shipowner of the Tongshun and Qian Fulin, the shipowner of the New Futai, were close friends, so they risked going to the scene of the accident to rescue the crew members. At that time, the crew members had already been rescued by Japanese ships, etc. After the Tongshun searched with its whistle, the Japanese ship Taizan Maru transferred the rescued people and the people rescued by the pilot boat to the Tongshun ship, which carried them to Shanghai. Yesterday afternoon, the Heping Company received a telegram from the Tongshun stating that it had rescued the crew members and was scheduled to arrive at Wusong this morning. It is estimated that it could sail into the Huangpu River and arrive safely in Shanghai before noon.

Sinking Ship Cannot Be Salvaged

According to the staff of the Heping Company who spoke to this reporter, the location of the New Futai's accident is between shallow sand and reefs, and ships cannot sail to that sea area. Therefore, the sunken ship and cargo cannot be salvaged. The New Futai Ship had a gross tonnage of 4,200 tons. When it was purchased, the ship price was 160,000 taels. The Zhongxing coal inside the ship was also worth 50,000 to 60,000 yuan. In addition to the clothes of the crew members and sailors, the total loss is 300,000 yuan. However, they had purchased 100,000 taels of peace insurance from Zhaotai and others. After the accident, Heping has reported to various insurance companies and sent personnel to Tongsha to inspect. At the same time, it has reported to the Jianghai Customs Port Affairs Director and the Shanghai Maritime Affairs Bureau.

Two Radiograms

After the New Futai ship sank in the Tongsha sea area, the Tongshun ship, which sailed to rescue it, sent two radiograms to Shanghai yesterday. The first telegram was sent at 10:40 AM, reporting that the surviving crew members of the New Futai were living on Sanjian Island and were currently being rescued and boarding the ship. The second telegram said that 17 people had been rescued from Sanjian Island, fearing that only this number of the 52 crew members of the New Futai had been rescued. In addition, three bodies were found. It is said that the shipowner, chief officer, engineer, and radio operator had all drowned. Please send someone to Wusong at dawn tomorrow to meet the rescued people. The ship will sail to Nanjing.

City Chamber of Commerce Requests Amendment to Stamp Tax Penalty Regulations

Allowing a reasonable period of hesitation after sentencing

Re-examination should be allowed if reasons for objection are presented

The Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce yesterday submitted a petition to the Ministry of Finance, stating: "Regarding the petition, on the 25th of this month, we received a joint letter from over one hundred trade associations, including the paper, woolen fabric, mercerized cotton weaving, sausage, mineral ash factory, cotton cloth, knitwear, department store, coal, silk and satin, clock and watch, gold, candle, and footwear industries, stating: 'We have learned that the stamp tax bureau's inspection of stamps has been reported by merchants that inspectors have been wantonly harassing, exceeding the scope of the stamp tax regulations, deliberately finding fault, and imposing heavy penalties everywhere. During store inspections, they often overturn boxes and ransack containers, searching at will. Even scraps of paper with temporary notes or memos with temporary numbers are copied and fined. When enforcing penalties, they often summon people to the bureau and order them to pay the fines immediately. Only after the fines are paid do they show the penalty receipts. Otherwise, they detain them. This is not the way to convince merchants. After discussing relief measures, the associations decided to petition the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce to forward the current stamp tax penalty rules to the Ministry of Finance, as they are prone to abuses and should be quickly amended.' The Ministry's instructions to the Shandong Stamp Tobacco and Alcohol Tax Bureau on September 14th included the province's original proposed procedures for inspection, stating that 'during inspections, whether of shops or residences, local police must be present, and the parties involved must be advised to hand over all books, contracts, etc., and that there should be no forceful entry into accounting rooms or arbitrary searches.' It was reported that 'after explaining the inspection section of the sixth item of the reply, it is still feasible.' The reports from the trade associations mentioned above stated that 'overturning boxes and ransacking containers, searching at will,' is tantamount to harassment. We propose that the Ministry circulate this instruction to all provinces for compliance to facilitate the people and merchants. As for the current Stamp Tax Regulation Review Committee, it originally conducts reviews in writing, and the parties concerned have no opportunity to appear and defend themselves. Once a penalty is imposed, they must be summoned to the bureau to forcibly pay the fine. Only after the fine is paid is the penalty receipt shown. Thus, even if the penalized party has reasons to defend themselves in accordance with the law, or if the case is actually due to the tax bureau's misapplication or misunderstanding, the fine has already been paid and cannot be changed. This penalty procedure is unfair. We propose that during the review, the person being reviewed should be notified in advance, and those who wish to appear and defend themselves should be allowed to do so, and those who do not wish to appear should not be forced. Alternatively, after the penalty is imposed, a reasonable period of hesitation should be allowed. If the penalized person presents objections and there are indeed reasons, the previous judgment may be reviewed and changed. Although this would add a step for the tax bureau, it would make the process easier to manage in detail. Therefore, we are submitting this document to the Ministry for review, hoping that you will adopt and implement it for the public good." We respectfully submit this to the Ministry of Finance.

They violated the rules and disregarded public opinion. For a time, the members of the association publicly opposed it in the newspapers, and the entire supervisory committee made a declaration of resignation. The standing committee's unauthorized change of name and illegal organizational actions have lost the trust of overseas Chinese merchants. The local government also does not value their actions. Therefore, the reported amendments to the constitution have not yet been approved. It is clear that such an unsound organization cannot represent public opinion. (The Sudong region has over ten thousand stores, but the association has less than three hundred members, including merchants or individuals from near and far, and less than half are major businesses.) The standing committee members colluded with the former consul Zuo Lin, and daily engaged in deceptive tactics for their own benefit. After Consul Liang arrived in Medan following Zuo's dismissal, the standing committee, having lost its protective amulet, became jealous and resentful, and engaged in planned sabotage. When the consulate was handling the handover, they incited delays and resistance. When the consulate initially discussed the consulate's financial difficulties, they ridiculed it as extortion for personal gain. When the consulate entrusted the handling of nationality registration, all overseas Chinese groups eagerly offered assistance, but the standing committee not only refused to accept it but also published it in newspapers and sent special letters to various ports to undermine it. When the consulate made preliminary negotiations with the local Sultan regarding the hawker incident, they instigated the People's Daily to publish articles attacking it. In another instance, when a small number of merchants established an association to collect a 30% refund of freight charges from shipping companies, Consul Liang, at the request of the merchants, inquired about suspected monopoly and fraud, and was accused of undermining public welfare. After the consulate received instructions from the Ministry of Industry and Commerce that the chamber of commerce should be re-elected on a regular basis in accordance with the law, they refused to respond. (It is said that the former Consul colluded with the consulate to conceal the report, and the consulate has no records to check.) There were countless such acts of framing. Although Consul Liang interacted with them daily, he could never gain their cooperation. Their prejudice was obvious. Because of the Ministry of Industry and Commerce's instructions, the standing committee passed a resolution on June 11th, instructing the standing committee to explain the reasons for the reorganization and renaming to the public. However, the standing committee violated the resolution and brazenly made a fierce declaration attacking the consulate, which was published in newspapers and distributed in leaflets on June 29th, defaming and slandering without reservation. At the same time, they also sent a secretary to beg the Dutch newspaper to publish slanderous articles (the Dutch newspaper stated that it was the association's secretary who orally reported it). Attacking from both within and without, they became a laughingstock to other countries. Public opinion was in an uproar, and the overseas Chinese were resentful. At that time, members of the association successively published denials in the newspapers, and even members of the supervisory committee held meetings to question Medan community groups and overseas Chinese businesses, and even launched a collective condemnation (the original newspaper has been attached to the Shanghai City Chamber of Commerce). The standing committee, being the target of public criticism, could not defend themselves. The standing committee, still unbridled, not only filed complaints everywhere but also colluded with Song Faxiang, the Consul General in Batavia, to protect their biases, causing social unrest. Members of the executive and supervisory committees, such as Chen Tianjiu, felt that the merchant organization was being used by a few people as a tool to humiliate the country, and the reputation of all members was swept away. Therefore, they successively published resignations in the newspapers. Currently, the chamber of commerce has become an organization with insufficient legal officers. Your association has been deceived and blindly followed suit, sending telegrams back and forth as if your association would be adversely affected if Consul Liang did not leave. Otherwise, why would you exert so much effort? In fact, your association has nothing to do with this case. In terms of scope, it is absolutely impossible to accept the transfer of control. Now, you have actually accepted the transfer of control and, without distinguishing right from wrong, immediately stated that Consul Liang published the statement of distrust of the chamber of commerce in the Dutch government's official newspaper, which is a disgrace to the country, in order to confirm his crime. In Medan, there are only two foreign business newspapers and no Dutch government official newspaper. We have also not seen Liang act in such an unseemly manner. It was the standing committee that sought to publish slanderous articles themselves. Who is humiliating the country? The truth is obvious. The overseas Chinese groups now consider the association's absurdity a great shame and insult. What will your association think when you hear about this? Can you send telegrams back and forth to protect the country's image and quell the overseas Chinese's public anger? In short, your association was unaware of the social situation in Medan, the content of the chamber of commerce, and the character of the standing committee, and rashly stepped in to open an unprecedented situation. This is the overseas Chinese group's great regret for your association. Your association is in a prominent position close to key officials. Do you really want to use your residual power to exert it overseas? Otherwise, how could you be so reckless? After Consul Liang was ordered to be dismissed, the overseas Chinese groups already felt that the Ministry of Foreign Affairs was reversing right and wrong and disregarding public opinion. Knowing that although petitions were sent, the situation was still isolated, and it was useless to retain him, we were determined not to interfere further. Now, we know that the authorities' resolute decision was due to the collusion of all the gentlemen of your association who acted as accomplices. Alas, the country has been in turmoil in recent years, and the political situation has been constantly changing. Now, the absurdity of your association is enough to prove it, and we cannot help but feel sorry for the party and the country's future. Consul Liang is deeply loved and respected by the overseas Chinese. Therefore, when he left Medan this time, over twenty overseas Chinese groups held a meeting to bid him farewell, and banquets were held every night to send him off. His virtue was praised in the southern region, and overseas Chinese sang praises. Silver tripods and shields were engraved to commemorate his protection of overseas Chinese, and they were presented one after another. On the eve of his departure, hundreds of people from party, government, industry, commerce, education, and newspaper circles lay down on the road to see him off. It was an unprecedented grand occasion in Medan. If Consul Liang had really oppressed overseas Chinese merchants, as your association claims, how could he have received such sincere support? (The original newspaper has also been attached to the association.) The overseas Chinese groups, driven by justice, have detailed the facts, hoping that your association will reflect on them. Please show us the four major points of accusation against Liang, so that the public can criticize them. We await your reply with the utmost urgency. In addition to sending copies to the Central Party Headquarters, the National Government, all courts, associations, and party, government, industry, commerce, education, and newspaper organizations at home and abroad, we respectfully ask you to review and clarify the truth and avoid being deceived by one-sided information. November 26, 1932."
